<p><strong>Bike Wheels</strong></p><p>Finding the right set of bike wheels can transform your
            cycling experience. Whether itâ€™s a deep-section carbon race wheel, a tough do-it-all
            gravel wheel, or something to see you through commuting in all seasons, at ProBikeKit
            we have wide range of wheelsets for all occasions.</p><p>As one of the bicycleâ€™s fundamental components, upgrading your
            wheels is perhaps the most significant investment you can make to your bike,
            and the one that will yield the biggest returns in performance. Whether your goal
            is to increase straight line speed, grip on loose surfaces, or simply comfort, having
            the right wheelset for the job is the place to start.</p><p><strong>Material Matters</strong></p><p>It can be daunting when setting out to find a new set of
            hoops for your pride and joy, there is seemingly a wheelset for all eventualities.
            Traditionally carbon bike wheels have the potential to be lighter and are designed
            to be more aerodynamically advantageous, but these performance benefits come at
            a (literal) price. However, if itâ€™s a wheel for racing, be that a criterium or
            road, or simply for going fast with your friends, then theyâ€™re the perfect addition
            to your bike. Alloy wheels, on the other hand, are typically more robust and
            economical. That isnâ€™t to say theyâ€™re inferior. It is still possible to get a high-quality
            alloy wheelset, which is the right choice for the task you have in mind. Itâ€™s a
            case of different spokes, for different folks.</p><p><strong>Whatâ€™s New</strong></p><p>Until recently, rim-brake bike wheels had been the most
            popular â€” if not, only â€” choice on road bikes. However, over the last few years
            disc brakesâ€™ popularity on the road has surged, and we are now seeing more wheel
            makers producing â€˜disc-brake onlyâ€™ models. Generally, rim brakes were lighter
            and easier to maintain than discs. But advances in disc brake technology has almost
            eroded this benefit-gap. Add to this the increased stopping power and
            all-weather reliability disc brakes offer, and itâ€™s easy to see why they have become
            the favored option for riders across all disciplines. Though it should be noted
            that mountain bike riders have been touting these benefits off road for many
            years!</p><p>Another bit of tech common off road, which is slowly gaining
            traction among road cyclists, is tubeless tires. Diehard pros may cling to
            tubular tires â€” which is apt since these tires are glued to the rim â€” for years
            to come, but the number of pros touting the performance advantages of tubeless tires
            is mounting. Tubeless tires, not only reduce the chance of a ride-stopping
            puncture, but also offer lower rolling resistance, translating into more speed
            for less effort. For the everyday cyclist, clincher tires, the traditional inner
            tube set up, still remains a popular choice, but as with disc brakes many manufacturers
            are now offering wheels as tubeless only.</p><p>

            wheels. Whether you want a wheelset for your road bike, mountain bike, or
